<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 12pt"><B>14. DISCONTINUED OPERATIONS</B>
</DIV>


<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;On February&nbsp;27, 2003, Penwest sold substantially all of the assets (the &#147;Assets&#148;) used in the
Company&#146;s excipient business to subsidiaries and affiliates of Josef Rettenmaier Holding GmbH &#038; Co.
KG (&#147;Rettenmaier&#148;) for $41.75&nbsp;million, plus the assumption of specified liabilities. The Assets of
the excipient business were sold to Rettenmaier, either directly or through the sale of the
outstanding capital stock of the three subsidiaries of Penwest that did business in the UK, Germany
and Finland. The purchase price included $39.5&nbsp;million in cash and a non-interest bearing
promissory note of $2.25&nbsp;million, with $1.0&nbsp;million paid to Penwest in April&nbsp;2003 and $1.25&nbsp;million
paid to Penwest in May&nbsp;2004.
</DIV>

<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;In 2003, the Company recorded a gain on the Asset Sale of approximately $9.9&nbsp;million (no tax
effect), and has reported the operating results of the excipient business as a discontinued
operation in accordance with SFAS No.&nbsp;144, &#147;Accounting for the Impairment or Disposal of Long-Lived
Assets.&#148; The net carrying amount of the assets and liabilities on the date of the Asset Sale was
approximately $29.5&nbsp;million. The approximate carrying values of the major classes were: property,
plant and equipment of $11.4&nbsp;million; inventory of $8.3&nbsp;million; receivables of $6.0&nbsp;million; and
intangible assets of $4.3&nbsp;million offset by other net liabilities. The gain on the Asset Sale is
net of transaction related costs totaling $3.1&nbsp;million, primarily consisting of professional and
advisory fees. Revenues and pretax profits for the excipient business approximated $6.1&nbsp;million and
$203,000, respectively, for the period January&nbsp;1, 2003 through the Asset Sale date of February&nbsp;27,
2003.
</DIV>

<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Prior to the sale of the excipient business, the Company owned its office, laboratory and
warehouse facility in Patterson, New York, as well as a facility in Cedar Rapids, Iowa, where it
manufactured pharmaceutical excipients. As part of the Asset Sale, the Company transferred these
properties and assigned its lease of a pharmaceutical excipient manufacturing facility in Nastola,
Finland to Rettenmaier. Under a lease agreement signed with Rettenmaier on February&nbsp;27, 2003, the
Company has the right to occupy approximately 14,000 square feet of office and research and
development space in the Patterson facility until February&nbsp;2008.
</DIV>

<P align="center" style="font-size: 10pt">F-23
</DIV>

<!-- PAGEBREAK -->
<P><HR noshade><P>

<DIV style="font-family: 'Times New Roman',Times,serif">

<DIV align="center" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 18pt">PENWEST PHARMACEUTICALS CO<BR>

<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 12pt"><B>15. LICENSING AGREEMENTS</B>
</DIV>


<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;The Company enters into collaborative arrangements with pharmaceutical companies to develop,
manufacture or market products formulated with its drug delivery technologies.
</DIV>

<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 12pt"><I>Endo Pharmaceuticals Inc.</I>
</DIV>


<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;In September&nbsp;1997, the Company entered into a strategic alliance agreement with Endo
Pharmaceuticals Inc. with respect to the development of oxymorphone ER, an extended release
formulation of oxymorphone, based on the Company&#146;s TIMERx technology. Oxymorphone ER is a narcotic
analgesic for the treatment of moderate to severe pain in patients requiring continuous
around-the-clock opioid therapy for an extended period of time. This agreement was amended and
restated in April&nbsp;2002. Endo has a broad product line including established brands such as
Lidoderm<SUP style="font-size: 85%; vertical-align: text-top">&#174;</SUP>, Percodan<SUP style="font-size: 85%; vertical-align: text-top">&#174;</SUP> and Percocet<SUP style="font-size: 85%; vertical-align: text-top">&#174;</SUP>. Endo is registered with the U.S. Drug Enforcement
Administration as a developer, manufacturer and marketer of controlled narcotic substances.
</DIV>

<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Under the strategic alliance agreement, the responsibilities of the Company and Endo with
respect to the oxymorphone product are determined by a committee comprised of an equal number of
members from each of the Company and Endo (the &#147;Alliance Committee&#148;). During the development of the
product, the Company formulated oxymorphone ER, and Endo conducted all clinical studies and
prepared and filed all regulatory applications. The Company has agreed to supply TIMERx material to
Endo, and Endo has agreed to manufacture and market oxymorphone ER in the United States. The
manufacture and marketing outside of the United States may be conducted by the Company, Endo or a
third party, as determined by the Alliance Committee.
</DIV>

<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Prior to April&nbsp;17, 2003, the Company shared with Endo the costs involved in the development
and pre-marketing of oxymorphone ER. On April&nbsp;17, 2003, the Company discontinued its participation
in the funding of the development and pre-marketing of oxymorphone ER. The Company took this
action because it believed that its strategic focus should be on funding other products in its
development pipeline. As a result of this termination of funding, Endo has the right to complete
the development of oxymorphone ER and recoup the portion of development and pre-marketing costs
incurred by Endo that otherwise would have been funded by the Company. Endo may recoup such
development costs through a temporary adjustment in the royalty rate payable to the Company, which
will return to its pre-adjustment level once Endo has recovered such costs. Endo may also allow
the Company to reimburse Endo directly for the unfunded amounts. The Company estimates that
through November&nbsp;30, 2005, these unfunded costs approximated $22.3&nbsp;million. The Company expects
these costs to increase as Endo incurs pre-launch marketing costs. The Company anticipates that if
oxymorphone ER receives approval from the FDA, that it may reimburse Endo for these unfunded costs
and resume funding marketing costs. The Company has agreed with Endo that the party marketing
oxymorphone ER will pay the other party royalties initially equal to 50% of the net realization, as
defined in the agreement between Endo and the Company, subject to adjustment for unfunded
development costs. This percentage will decrease if the aggregate U.S. net realization exceeds
pre-determined thresholds. In general, the royalty payable by the marketing party to the other
party will not drop below 40%. However, the royalty will be reduced by one-third in limited
circumstances, including termination of the agreement based on uncured material breaches of the
agreement by the royalty receiving party and specified bankruptcy and insolvency events involving
the royalty receiving party. Under the agreement, Endo will purchase formulated TIMERx material
for use in oxymorphone ER exclusively from the Company at specified prices, and include these
purchases in cost of goods sold of the product prior to determining net realization, on which the
royalty payment is calculated.
</DIV>

<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 12pt"><I>Mylan Pharmaceuticals Inc.</I>
</DIV>


<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;On March&nbsp;2, 2000, Mylan announced that it had signed a supply and distribution agreement with
Pfizer to market a generic version of all three strengths (30 mg, 60 mg, 90 mg) of Pfizer&#146;s
Procardia XL. In connection with
</DIV>

<P align="center" style="font-size: 10pt">F-24
</DIV>

<!-- PAGEBREAK -->
<P><HR noshade><P>
<H5 align="left" style="page-break-before:always"><A HREF="#tocpage">Table of Contents</A></H5><P>

<DIV style="font-family: 'Times New Roman',Times,serif">

<DIV align="center" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 18pt">PENWEST PHARMACEUTICALS CO<BR>
NOTES TO CONSOLIDATED FINANCIAL STATEMENTS (continued)
</DIV>

<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt">that agreement, Mylan decided not to market Nifedipine XL, a product the Company had developed
in collaboration with Mylan, and agreed to pay Penwest a royalty on all future net sales of the 30
mg strength of Pfizer&#146;s generic version of Procardia XL. The royalty percentage was comparable to
the percentage called for in Penwest&#146;s original agreement with Mylan for Nifedipine XL. Mylan has
retained the marketing rights to the 30 mg strength of Nifedipine XL. Mylan&#146;s sales in the United
States in 2005 of the 30 mg strength of Pfizer&#146;s generic version of Procardia XL totaled
approximately $32.9&nbsp;million. The term of this agreement continues until such time as Mylan
permanently ceases to market the generic version of Procardia XL. In 2005, 2004 and 2003, royalties
from Mylan were approximately $3.9&nbsp;million, $4.8&nbsp;million and $4.1&nbsp;million, respectively, or 63%,
94% and 88%, respectively, of the Company&#146;s total revenue from continuing operations.
</DIV>


<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 12pt"><I>Prism Pharmaceuticals, Inc.</I>
</DIV>


<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;On April&nbsp;26, 2005, the Company entered into a licensing agreement (the &#147;License Agreement&#148;)
with Prism Pharmaceuticals, Inc. (&#147;Prism&#148;) granting Prism exclusive rights to market Penwest&#146;s
PW2101 product in the United States and Canada. Under the terms of the License Agreement, Penwest
granted Prism an exclusive license under certain Penwest intellectual property to develop, make,
use and commercialize PW2101 in the United States and Canada for all indications except the
treatment and/or prophylaxis of migraine. Prism made a non-refundable $4.0&nbsp;million payment to the
Company upon signing the License Agreement and had agreed to pay Penwest milestone payments upon
achievement of milestones related to FDA approval and launch of PW2101, and royalties on net sales.
Upon receipt, the Company deferred the $4.0&nbsp;million received from Prism.
</DIV>

<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;In June&nbsp;2005, the FDA issued a non approvable letter for the Company&#146;s NDA for PW2101. Given
the FDA&#146;s concerns expressed in the non approvable letter, the time and resources the Company
expected it would take to address them, and the commercial window for this product opportunity,
Penwest decided not to undertake the additional activities on PW2101 that it believed would be
required to address the FDA&#146;s concerns. On July&nbsp;7, 2005, the Company was notified by Prism that
Prism also did not intend to proceed with development activities on PW2101 under the License
Agreement. As a result, the License Agreement terminated effective July&nbsp;20, 2005. In connection
with the termination, Penwest and Prism signed a settlement agreement in September&nbsp;2005, and
Penwest repaid Prism $1.75&nbsp;million of the $4.0&nbsp;million payment Penwest received from Prism, and
recognized the remaining $2.25&nbsp;million as licensing fee revenue in the third quarter of 2005.
</DIV>

<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 12pt"><B>16. CONTINGENCIES</B>
</DIV>


<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Substantial patent litigation exists in the pharmaceutical industry. Patent litigation
generally involves complex legal and factual questions, and the outcome frequently is difficult to
predict. An unfavorable outcome in any patent litigation affecting the Company could cause the
Company to pay substantial damages, alter its products or processes, obtain licenses and/or cease
certain activities. Even if the outcome is favorable to the Company, the Company could incur
substantial litigation costs.
</DIV>

<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;The Company is a party to certain claims and proceedings in the ordinary course of business.
The Company does not believe any of these matters will result, individually or in the aggregate, in
a material adverse effect upon its financial condition or future
results of operations.
</DIV>

<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 12pt"><B>17. RELATED PARTY TRANSACTIONS</B>
</DIV>


<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Under a Recognition and Incentive Agreement (as amended, the &#147;Baichwal Agreement&#148;) with Anand
Baichwal, the Company&#146;s Senior Vice President of Licensing and Chief Scientific Officer, the
Company is obligated to pay to Dr.&nbsp;Baichwal on an annual basis in arrears, royalties for (i)
one-half of one percent of the Company&#146;s Net Sales (as defined in the Baichwal Agreement) of
TIMERx<SUP style="font-size: 85%; vertical-align: text-top">&#174;</SUP> Material (as defined in the Baichwal Agreement) to third parties, (ii)&nbsp;one-half of one
percent of royalties received by the Company under licenses, collaborations or other exploitation
</DIV>

<P align="center" style="font-size: 10pt">F-25
</DIV>

</DIV>

<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt">agreements with third parties with respect to the sale, license, use or exploitation by such
third parties of products based on or incorporating the TIMERx<SUP style="font-size: 85%; vertical-align: text-top">&#174;</SUP> Material, and (iii)&nbsp;one-half of one
percent of payments made in lieu of such Net Sales or royalties and received by the Company. Such
payments cease in the event that Dr.&nbsp;Baichwal&#146;s employment is terminated for cause. The Baichwal
Agreement also contains non-competition and non-solicitation provisions that expire two years after
the termination of Dr.&nbsp;Baichwal&#146;s employment. These royalties for Dr.&nbsp;Baichwal totaled
approximately $20,000, $25,000 and $23,000 for 2005, 2004 and 2003, respectively.
</DIV>


<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Under a Royalty Agreement with John N. Staniforth (the &#147;Staniforth Agreement&#148;), a member of
the Company&#146;s Board of Directors, the Company is obligated to pay Dr.&nbsp;Staniforth on an annual basis
in arrears one-half of one percent of the Company&#146;s Net Sales (as defined in the Staniforth
Agreement) of TIMERx<SUP style="font-size: 85%; vertical-align: text-top">&#174;</SUP> Material (as defined in the Staniforth Agreement) related to the products
covered by the TIMERx<SUP style="font-size: 85%; vertical-align: text-top">&#174;</SUP> patents. These royalties for Dr.&nbsp;Staniforth totaled approximately $20,000,
$25,000 and $23,000 for 2005, 2004 and 2003, respectively.
</DIV>

<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Dr.&nbsp;Staniforth also has a consulting agreement with the Company under which he is paid $80,000
per year, payable in quarterly payments. The consulting agreement is automatically renewed each
year and is cancelable by either the Company or Dr.&nbsp;Staniforth upon thirty days&#146; prior notice. Any
invention that results from this consulting agreement is legally owned by Penwest. Dr.&nbsp;Staniforth
also serves on the Scientific Advisory Board of the Company and is paid $1,500 for each meeting
attended.
</DIV>
